POV: Iphone fanboi tests a samsung
The S24+ 512GB seems like a better flagship than the Ultra to me, f you don't need the mega-zoom camera on the Ultra, the 1TB storage or the S Pen. The rounded corners look much nicer and are smother to hold in your palm than the square corners of the Ultra. The S24+ is 36g (~16%) lighter than the Ultra at 196g vs 232g. It has the same screen brightness and resolution at a slightly more managable size, resulting in better pixel density (ppi) than the Ultra, so everything will look better. The S24+ is also 3.8mm shorter, 3.1mm narrower width, and a whopping 0.9mm thinner, whilst only sacrificing 100mAh battery. This weight and size difference translates to huge quality of life and usability improvements when using your phone in bed for example, holding it above your face, or sideways.   The only real loss I'd say is the lack of Gorilla Glass Armor on the Ultra, with the same old Gorilla Glass Victus 2 on the S24+. Gorilla Glass Victus 2 suffers heavily from micro-scratches, more than the last few versions of Gorilla Glass. They significantly sacrificed scratch protection for drop protection with Victus 2. It seems like Gorilla Glass Armor makes it so you don't ever need to worry about a screen protector, and a case would only be to protect against minor scratches/dents on the back and sides from drops. You could probably use the S24 Ultra completely naked (without a screen protector or case), which is exciting.  Hopefully next year, across the whole range (S25, S25+ and S25 Ultra), they add Gorilla Glass Armor and upgrade the maximum storage to at least 1TB. I'd also like to see them include the flagship camera setup across the sizes and just continue the Ultra for people who want the S Pen and biggest screen. I'd also like 1440p resolution on the S24 base model for maximum pixel density (ppi), even though this would negatively affect battery life it would be nice to have the choice.

The "Always On Display" feature is a very good example of this. Using USB Type C ports is another recent example. Very few features on the iPhones are original features that Apple pioneered. That hard square edge is something that NUMEROUS reviewers have complained about.  And speaking of the new edge, this phone uses a titanium edge. But Apple didn't come up with that idea either. Apple COPIED  it from a British phone maker called "VERTU." VERTU designed a phone in 2007 that used titanium called the "Asent Ti." So no, Apple didn't come up with using titanium in a smartphone.   If we go to laptops, THEN Apple's MacBook M-series SoCs are cutting edge and revolutionary in many ways, but wait for it, wait for it; Apple based the M-series design on the ARM architecture, which was invented by "Acorn Computers." Apple purchased the rights to use the ARM SoC design well over a decade ago, and has since modified it. So Apple's vaunted M-series SoCs are not even their original idea or design lol. So why wouldn't all this ai be possible on a s23 ultra?
Many of the features that are marketed as "AI" have nothing to do with AI. Like for example when selecting a part of the screen and searching for the thing on your display in google, that's searching is handled by google. The phono just has to crop the photo and give it to google to do the heavy lifting. Also when you moved that person playing basketball, I am pretty convinced it's not AI either. They're just doing an edge detection filter to select just the player and doing some content aware filling. I may be wrong but the main point is that people become mesmerized when hearing the term "AI" so companies capitalize on that and market a lot of their features as AI when in reality, plain old algorithmic solution are better, they generally are computationally more efficient and produce the correct result more often than AI. I hope you make a video on that to educate people on this and point out than AI is not THE best solution for everything.
